language:1 abstract:1 bibcom:1 front:1 article:1

abstract:1 bibcom:1 front:1 article:1
</FONT><FONT FACE="Verdana, Arial" SIZE=2>A polysaccharide-rich fraction (ATF) of medicinal mushroom <I>Agaricus brasiliensis</I> was evaluated on the candidacidal activity, H<SUB>2</SUB>O<SUB>2</SUB> and nitric oxide (NO) production, and expression of mannose receptors by murine peritoneal macrophages. Mice received three intraperitoneal (i.p.) injections of ATF and after 48 h their peritoneal resident macrophages were assayed against <I>Candida albicans</I> yeast forms. The treatment increased fungicidal activity and it was associated with higher levels of H<SUB>2</SUB>O<SUB>2</SUB>, whereas NO production was not affected. We also found that the treatment enhances mannose receptor expression by peritoneal macrophages, which are involved in the attachment and phagocytosis of non-opsonized microorganisms. Treatment of animals with ATF was able to enhance the clearance of <I>C. albicans</I> during the first 6 h after the experimental i.p. infection. Our results suggest that this extract can increase host resistance against some infectious agents through the stimulation of microbicidal activity of macrophages. </FONT><FONT FACE="Arial" COLOR="#000080">
